## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration typically depends on position (restoring force, possibly nonlinear), velocity (damping), and time (external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, and driven-damped oscillators are the primary candidates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with periodic drive)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Cubic + quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring)
- Driven van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping (velocity-dependent): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * v (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Driven with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (general driven damped linear)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → symmetric potential wells
- Even-power terms (x²) break symmetry → asymmetric oscillation and can indicate shifted equilibria
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (self-sustained oscillations, van der Pol type)
- Periodic explicit time dependence (sin/cos of t) indicates external driving forces → look for resonance phenomena
- Product terms x*v suggest velocity-dependent forces that change sign with position → energy exchange mechanisms
- Cubic position terms (x³) with opposite sign to linear term (x) indicate double-well or hardening/softening spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests autonomous system → energy conservation or dissipation without external input
- Odd powers of velocity (v, v³) represent dissipative forces; even powers (v²) represent direction-dependent drag

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

The GT has three key components:
1. A term proportional to `x*exp(-|x|)` (depends on x)
2. A term proportional to `log(|v| + 1)` (depends on v)
3. A term proportional to `sin(t)` (depends on t)

Let me analyze the candidates systematically. Most candidates use `tanh(c1*x)` for the x-dependence, which cannot match `x*exp(-|x|)` since tanh has fundamentally different behavior. Many candidates also lack proper v-dependence (needing `log(|v|+1)`).

Let me focus on candidates that have both v-dependence AND x-dependence beyond just tanh:

**Candidate 37:** `c0*tanh(c1*x + c2) + c3*t + c4*v + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7*log(c8*x**2 + c9)`
- x-dependence: tanh + log(x²+const) — cannot produce x*exp(-|x|)
- v-dependence: linear c4*v — cannot produce log(|v|+1)
- No match.

**Candidate 41:** `c0*tanh(c1*x) + c2 + c3*cos(c4 + t) + c5/(c6 + t) + c7*log(c8*x**2 + c9*v**2 + 1)`
- Has `log(c8*x² + c9*v² + 1)` which mixes x and v — cannot separate into `x*exp(-|x|) + log(|v|+1)`
- No match.

**Candidate 50:** `c0*tanh(c1*x + c2) + c3*t + c4*v + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7*log(c8*v**2 + c9)`
- v-dependence: c4*v + c7*log(c8*v² + c9). Setting c4=0, this becomes c7*log(c8*v² + c9). For this to equal -0.4456*log(|v|+1), we'd need log(c8*v²+c9) ∝ log(|v|+1). But log(c8*v²+c9) = log(c8(v²+c9/c8)). This equals log of a quadratic in v, not log(|v|+1).
- x-dependence: tanh — cannot produce x*exp(-|x|)
- No match.

**Candidate 24:** `c0*tanh(c1*x) + c2 + c3*cos(c4 + t) + c5*t/(c6 + t) + c7*x*exp(c8*v)`
- Has x*exp(c8*v) — mixes x and v, not what we need.
- No match.

**Candidate 44:** `c0*tanh(c1*x) + c2*cos(c3 + t) + c4*t/(c5 + t) + c6*t*(c7 + v)**c8`
- v-dependence through t*(v+c7)^c8 — mixes t and v.
- No match.

None of the candidates have `x*exp(-|x|)` or equivalent x-dependence. All use `tanh(c1*x)` for x-dependence, which saturates at ±1 for large |x|, while `x*exp(-|x|)` decays to 0. These are fundamentally different functions — no parameter choice can make tanh equal to x*exp(-|x|).

Similarly, none of the candidates have `log(|v|+1)` — most have either linear v terms, exp(v) terms, or no v-dependence at all.

Since no candidate can simultaneously reproduce:
- The x-dependence: `x*exp(-|x|)`
- The v-dependence: `log(|v|+1)`
- The t-dependence: `sin(t)`

No candidate matches the GT.

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-1.1449635767559*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.445567501246416*log(Abs(v) + 1) + 0.10853689295113*sin(t)`

Key components of GT:
1. **x-dependent term:** `x*exp(-Abs(x))` — this is an odd-like function that decays exponentially
2. **v-dependent term:** `log(Abs(v) + 1)` — since v ≤ 0 on this domain, `Abs(v) = -v`, so this is `log(-v + 1)` = `log(1 - v)`
3. **t-dependent term:** `sin(t)` — pure sinusoidal, no other t-dependence

**Critical observations:**
- The GT has NO terms that are rational functions of t (like `t/(a+t)`), NO `log(t+1)` terms, NO `exp(t)` terms, NO linear terms in t or v alone.
- The x-dependence is `x*exp(-|x|)`, which is NOT equivalent to `tanh(x)`. While both are odd and bounded, `tanh(x) → ±1` as `x → ±∞`, but `x*exp(-|x|) → 0` as `x → ±∞`. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

Let me verify: `tanh(x)` approaches ±1 for large |x|, while `x*exp(-|x|)` approaches 0. These are linearly independent functions and no constant multiple of `tanh(c1*x)` can equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x.

Since **every single candidate** contains `tanh(c1*x)` (or `tanh(c1*x + c2)`) as the x-dependent term, and the GT requires `x*exp(-|x|)`, none of them can match the GT's x-dependence.

Additionally, almost all candidates contain t-dependent terms like `t/(c+t)`, `log(c*t+1)`, `exp(c*t)`, or linear `c*t` terms that cannot be made to equal zero while simultaneously matching the `sin(t)` component (since setting those coefficients to zero would leave only `cos(c+t)` for the t-dependence, which could match `sin(t)` via phase shift, but the x-dependence still fails).

Even if we could zero out the spurious t-terms, the fundamental mismatch in x-dependence (`tanh` vs `x*exp(-|x|)`) means no candidate can match.

Let me verify each candidate's verdict:

Candidates 1-50: All contain `tanh(c1*x)` as the primary x-dependent basis function. Since `tanh(c1*x)` and `x*exp(-|x|)` are linearly independent (different asymptotic behavior), no choice of constants can make `tanh(c1*x)` equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x. Therefore, none match.
